The 2026-05-27 cluster reflects the design-architecture decision cycle that produced the Section 5 architecture; the 2026-05-28 cluster reflects the operational and audience decision cycle that absorbed the Sections 8/9, 10, and 2 adversarial reviews.

### A.2 Thematic groupings

#### Identity, trust graph, and cryptographic envelope

- [D0003](decisions/D0003-implementation-language.md) — Rust core + Kotlin UI via UniFFI: the implementation substrate for capability tokens, Shamir reconstruction with memory hygiene, and the trust-graph operation envelope.
- [D0006](decisions/D0006-cryptographic-envelope.md) — COSE_Sign1 + deterministic CBOR encoding; the nine-field signed-operation schema with prior-hash chain and issuer-cert-hash binding; five operation types (attestation, attestation withdrawal, key-compromise revocation, introduction, key rotation) with the withdrawal-vs-compromise split closing the cascade-laundering attack; cascade quarantine semantics and 90-day stale-flag escalation.
- [D0007](decisions/D0007-multi-device.md) — Multi-device commitment demoted from v1/v2 architectural claim to v1 single-device-per-identity at the client level, with the schema-level multi-device support preserved as forward-compatibility for v2+ work.

#### Recovery

- [D0005](decisions/D0005-peer-verification.md) — Recovery peer-verification mechanism: pre-shared challenges (peer-selected questions answered out-of-band at provisioning) plus 48-hour delay-and-confirm window; calibrated to raise the cost of the unlock → peer enumeration → impersonation chain.
- [D0014](decisions/D0014-non-peer-recovery.md) — Non-peer recovery path: out of scope for v1 with explicit acknowledgment of the audience populations excluded; candidate v1.x/v2 paths named (printed paper shares held by self; time-locked self-recovery; single-trustee with attorney-client privilege; explicit no-recovery option).

#### Scope, audience, and roadmap

- [D0002](decisions/D0002-duress-profile.md) — Duress profile out of v1 (detected concealment is itself prosecutable in compelled-decryption jurisdictions); duress-wipe pattern deferred to v1.5 with the architectural-answer-to-compelled-unlock framing in §3.5.
- [D0004](decisions/D0004-v1-scope-cuts.md) — v1 scope cuts: Briar and reproducible builds deferred to v1.5; local CRDT dropped permanently; v1 UX narrowed to what one developer can ship soundly given §5's architectural scope.
- [D0007](decisions/D0007-multi-device.md) — Single-device-per-identity scope.
- [D0014](decisions/D0014-non-peer-recovery.md) — v1 audience scope as a function of recovery-architecture serviceability.

#### Implementation

- [D0001](decisions/D0001-project-name.md) — Working name (Cairn) per the brand-axis selection criteria; trademark and namespace checks tracked as Q2 outstanding follow-ups.
- [D0003](decisions/D0003-implementation-language.md) — Implementation-language stack and UniFFI binding-layer choice; subsumes earlier Q8 architectural-shape items.

#### Release security, audit, and assurance

- [D0011](decisions/D0011-audit-budget-and-timing.md) — Two-stage audit: pre-pilot cryptographic-primitives audit (Phase B gate, ~$15–30K subsidized; specific routes per OTF Secure Audit, Cure53 mission rates, NLnet NGI Zero Trust) plus pre-beta full audit (Phase C gate, $60–220K depending on firm selection). Subsidy programs named; firm selection deferred to Q7.
- [D0015](decisions/D0015-v1-release-security-posture.md) — v1 release-security posture: developer Sigstore identity signing + Rekor transparency log + Sigsum-anchored release log with witness cosignatures + multi-channel distribution through F-Droid (primary), Accrescent, and direct download + developer source review. The recruited 5+/3-of-5 reviewer pool with 3-of-5 attestation threshold defers from v1 critical path to v1.5 alongside reproducible Android builds; the combination delivers binary-equivalence multi-party verification at v1.5.

#### Operations, governance, and contingency

- [D0008](decisions/D0008-volunteer-baseline-cadence.md) — Release cadence as slippage acceptance: ships when 3-of-5 attestation forms (at v1.5+; v1 cadence governed by engineering+audit+consent gates per D0015); expected median 4–6 months at volunteer baseline; quarterly as post-honoraria operational target.
- [D0009](decisions/D0009-sudden-unavailability.md) — Sudden-developer-unavailability contingency: monthly dead-man's-switch check-in; pre-arranged partner advisory authority triggered at 60-day silence; pre-staged successor documentation. Partner advisory authority becomes permanent governance scaffold under D0016 deferral rather than transitional state.
- [D0010](decisions/D0010-foundation-jurisdiction.md) — Foundation jurisdiction as placeholder pending legal consultation; fiscal-sponsor stage as permanent grant-receipt structure under D0016 deferral; factual corrections to earlier Signal Foundation and Briar references; named diligence considerations to address if D0016 trigger activates.
- [D0012](decisions/D0012-researcher-safe-harbor.md) — Researcher protection as stated intent indefinitely under D0016 deferral; formalization through a standard Safe Harbor template (disclose.io, Bugcrowd "We Will Not Sue", EFF Coders' Rights Project) _if_ D0016 trigger activates and project incorporates; explicit acknowledgment of natural-person non-enforceability.
- [D0013](decisions/D0013-pilot-consent-exit.md) — Pilot consent and exit protocol modeled on IRB-equivalent protective-technology study practice; partner-mediated reporting channel as Phase B precondition; mid-pilot exit and tool-mediated harm reporting paths.
- [D0015](decisions/D0015-v1-release-security-posture.md) — v1 release-security posture: developer signing + Rekor transparency log + Sigsum-anchored release log + witness cosignatures + multi-channel distribution (F-Droid primary). The recruited 5+/3-of-5 reviewer pool defers to v1.5 alongside reproducible builds.
- [D0016](decisions/D0016-foundation-incorporation-trigger.md) — Foundation incorporation deferred from v1 / Phase C scope with v1.5 broader-release evaluation trigger. Five trigger criteria (pilot evidence; funding scale; funder requirement; personal-liability scenario; structural-mitigation cascade) with two-of-five activation threshold. Fiscal-sponsor arrangement as permanent grant-receipt structure for duration of deferral.

### A.3 Decision interactions

Several decisions interlock and are best read together. The principal chains:

- **Foundation-incorporation chain (deferred per D0016).** [D0016](decisions/D0016-foundation-incorporation-trigger.md) defers foundation incorporation from v1 / Phase C scope with a v1.5 broader-release evaluation trigger. If the trigger activates: [D0010](decisions/D0010-foundation-jurisdiction.md) (jurisdictional analysis substrate) becomes operational; [D0012](decisions/D0012-researcher-safe-harbor.md) Safe Harbor formalization proceeds; the §8.5 audit-disclosure posture shifts toward foundation-bound governance for broader-release users; [D0011](decisions/D0011-audit-budget-and-timing.md) Phase C funding for incorporation depends on Phase B legal-consultation work D0010 references. If the trigger does not activate: D0009 partner advisory authority becomes permanent governance scaffold; D0012 Safe Harbor remains published-preference indefinitely; fiscal-sponsor arrangement per D0010 is the permanent grant-receipt structure. Trigger non-activation is the expected outcome under several plausible operational trajectories per D0016.
- **Volunteer-baseline operations chain.** [D0008](decisions/D0008-volunteer-baseline-cadence.md) (release cadence as slippage acceptance) interacts with [D0009](decisions/D0009-sudden-unavailability.md) (sudden-unavailability contingency), [D0015](decisions/D0015-v1-release-security-posture.md) (v1 release-security cadence decoupled from pool quorum), and the §8.2 reviewer-honoraria operating model. At the volunteer baseline, the project's operational tempo is slower than the brief's earlier drafts assumed; D0015 brings the v1 release-cadence framing into alignment with the volunteer-baseline reality by removing pool quorum as a v1 gate. [D0013](decisions/D0013-pilot-consent-exit.md) pilot deployment is gated on the partner-mediation arrangement that itself depends on the §8.6 partner outreach D0008 makes operationally honest about the cadence of.
- **Recovery and audience-honesty chain.** [D0005](decisions/D0005-peer-verification.md) defines the peer-verification mechanism for users who have a peer network; [D0014](decisions/D0014-non-peer-recovery.md) acknowledges the populations whose threat condition precludes the peer-network precondition and commits to v1.x/v2 candidate paths for them. The §2.2 audience honesty extension and the §6.3 pilot-scope explicit exclusion both reflect this pairing.
- **Implementation-substrate chain.** [D0003](decisions/D0003-implementation-language.md) (Rust + Kotlin via UniFFI) is the implementation substrate that [D0006](decisions/D0006-cryptographic-envelope.md) (envelope construction) and [D0005](decisions/D0005-peer-verification.md) (recovery memory hygiene) commit to specifically. [D0007](decisions/D0007-multi-device.md) is the schema-level forward-compatibility commitment that v1's single-device deployment is built against.
- **Release-security v1-to-v1.5 chain.** [D0015](decisions/D0015-v1-release-security-posture.md) (v1 release-security posture: developer signed + public log + multi-channel; recruited pool deferred) interacts with [D0004](decisions/D0004-v1-scope-cuts.md) (reproducible builds also deferred to v1.5) and [D0011](decisions/D0011-audit-budget-and-timing.md) (pre-beta audit scope at v1.5 covers the release-security stack including the recruited pool). The chain reframes the §4.3 four-commitment differentiation as three commitments + a v1 release-security posture aligned with comparable open-source security tools, with v1.5 lifting the release-security posture to additionally-distinct via the recruited-pool + reproducible-builds combination.
- **Pilot-readiness chain.** v1 pilot deployment is gated on three Phase B items per the brief: the pre-pilot cryptographic-primitives audit per [D0011](decisions/D0011-audit-budget-and-timing.md); the partner-mediated consent and exit protocol per [D0013](decisions/D0013-pilot-consent-exit.md); and developer source review of v1 release candidates per [D0015](decisions/D0015-v1-release-security-posture.md) (the recruited pool quorum formation that earlier drafts named is no longer a v1 ship-gate). None is solely engineering-sequenced; each has its own funding or partner gate.

### A.4 What is not in the decision register

The brief contains operational and architectural choices that are documented in prose rather than as standalone decision records — for example, specific cryptographic primitive selections (Ed25519, Curve25519, ChaCha20-Poly1305, Shamir 3-of-5 default), the choice of Tor as the network anonymization layer, the GrapheneOS-on-Pixel platform baseline, the choice not to federate, and the no-skip-the-audit posture for broader-than-pilot release. These reflect standard practice or industry-consensus choices the brief documents in §§4, 5, and 8 rather than treating as project-specific decisions requiring an ADR. The register is reserved for choices where the project considered substantive alternatives and where future readers benefit from understanding why specific options were rejected.

Open questions in [open-questions.md](open-questions.md) (Q1–Q26) track decisions not yet made; resolved questions move to the decision register here. The interlock is one-directional: a decision document never references an open question as still-open if the decision document itself resolves it — the question is marked resolved at the time the decision document is written.

---

## Appendix B: Glossary

_Purpose: define terminology used in the brief for readers whose primary expertise sits in only one of the three audiences the brief addresses (cryptographic and security review; civil-society operational practice; civil-society and digital-rights grantmaking). Terms are organized thematically with alphabetical ordering within each group; cross-references use the Cairn-style "see X" convention._

### B.1 Cryptographic primitives, protocols, and standards

- **Authenticated encryption.** Encryption that simultaneously protects confidentiality and integrity, so that any tampering with the ciphertext is detectable on decryption. Cairn uses ChaCha20-Poly1305 (an AEAD construction) for symmetric authenticated encryption at multiple layers.
- **CBOR (Concise Binary Object Representation, RFC 8949).** A binary serialization format used by COSE and by Cairn's trust-graph operation envelope. _Deterministic CBOR_ refers to the canonical encoding rules in RFC 8949 §4.2.1 that guarantee a given data structure has exactly one valid byte sequence — necessary for cryptographic signing over CBOR to be reproducible across implementations.
- **ChaCha20-Poly1305.** A widely-deployed authenticated encryption scheme combining the ChaCha20 stream cipher with the Poly1305 message authentication code. Standardized in RFC 8439.
- **COSE (CBOR Object Signing and Encryption, RFC 9052).** A standard for cryptographic signing and encryption of CBOR-encoded data. Cairn's capability tokens and trust-graph operation envelopes are COSE_Sign1 structures (single-signer signed CBOR) per [D0006](decisions/D0006-cryptographic-envelope.md).
- **Curve25519.** An elliptic curve used for Diffie-Hellman key agreement (X25519). Cairn uses Curve25519 for ephemeral key agreement at the messaging-protocol layer (inherited from SimpleX's double-ratchet derivative).
- **Double ratchet.** A cryptographic protocol introduced by the Signal Protocol that provides forward secrecy and post-compromise security for ongoing message conversations through periodic key derivation. SimpleX uses a double-ratchet derivative for on-wire content protection.
- **Ed25519.** A high-performance elliptic-curve digital signature algorithm standardized in RFC 8032. Cairn's identity keypairs and trust-graph operation signatures are Ed25519.
- **Forward secrecy (FS).** A security property of a protocol where compromise of long-term keys does not allow decryption of past traffic. Each session key is derived freshly and used briefly; past sessions remain confidential after key compromise.
- **MLS (Messaging Layer Security, RFC 9420).** An IETF standard for group end-to-end encrypted messaging with forward secrecy and post-compromise security at group scale. Matrix has been migrating to MLS through 2024–2025.
- **OIDC (OpenID Connect).** An identity layer built on top of OAuth 2.0 that allows a relying party to verify the identity of an end user based on authentication performed by an authorization server. Sigstore's Fulcio binds release-signing certificates to OIDC identities, making the OIDC provider a trust placement in Cairn's release-security stack (§3.4, [Q11](open-questions.md)).
- **Post-compromise security (PCS).** A security property of a protocol where compromise of a session key does not allow decryption of subsequent traffic once a key-derivation step has occurred. PCS bounds forward damage; FS bounds backward damage.
- **Rekor.** Sigstore's append-only transparency log of code-signing events; the public record that Sigstore signatures land in. Operated as a single-operator log infrastructure by the Sigstore project (§4.1 dependency surface).
- **Shamir Secret Sharing (SSS).** A threshold cryptography scheme that splits a secret into N shares such that any K of them can reconstruct the secret while fewer than K reveal nothing about it. Cairn uses 3-of-5 SSS by default to split the master identity seed across recovery peers.
- **Sigstore.** A signing infrastructure stack (Fulcio for certificate issuance bound to OIDC; Rekor for transparency logging; cosign for signing operations) developed by the Linux Foundation. Cairn uses Sigstore for per-release identity-based signing on top of the Android APK signing key (§5.5).
- **Sigsum.** A minimalist, witness-cosigned transparency log infrastructure designed for sustainable multi-year operation. Cairn anchors its trust-graph operations and release attestations in Sigsum as commitments (hashes of operations, not operation content) (§5.2, §5.5).
- **Threshold cryptography.** Cryptographic schemes where a secret operation requires the cooperation of a threshold subset of N parties. Shamir Secret Sharing is one threshold-cryptography construction; threshold signatures (e.g., FROST) are another.
- **Transparency log.** An append-only public log of cryptographic events (signatures, attestations, certificates) maintained so that any party can verify the log is consistent and detect when it has been tampered with. Sigstore's Rekor and Sigsum are both transparency-log infrastructures with different operational models.

### B.2 Architecture concepts (Cairn-specific)

- **Attestation.** A signed statement by one user that another user's keypair, role, or context-specific property holds at a moment in time. Cairn's trust graph is built from attestations and the operations that modify them (revocation, introduction, key rotation per [D0006](decisions/D0006-cryptographic-envelope.md)).
- **Capability token.** A signed object that authorizes a specific operation by a specific device on behalf of an operational identity, scoped to a specific purpose (e.g., `messaging-send`, `trust-graph-attest`). Cairn's capability tokens are COSE_Sign1 structures with deterministic CBOR encoding.
- **Cascade quarantine.** The set of behaviors that propagate downstream of a trust-graph revocation. _Attestation withdrawal_ soft-flags downstream attestations from the withdrawal date forward (the attestation may have been honest at the time but is no longer endorsed); _key compromise revocation_ hard-suspends post-`revoked_as_of` attestations and soft-flags prior ones (see §5.2 and D0006). The split between withdrawal and compromise revocation closes the cascade-laundering attack identified in the §5 adversarial review.
- **Commitment-only anchoring.** The Sigsum integration pattern where the project logs only cryptographic commitments (hashes) of trust-graph operations rather than operation content. Issuer/subject/context stay out of public view; the log can still be used to detect tampering or rollback of the operation history (§5.2).
- **Cryptographic identity.** A keypair that represents a user's persistent identity, bound to operations the user performs cryptographically. Cairn uses a three-tier identity model: master identity (off-device in routine operation; Shamir-split among recovery peers); operational identity (hardware-element-gated; signs day-to-day operations); device-scoped capability tokens (signed by the operational identity to authorize specific device operations).
- **Five operation types.** The trust-graph operations Cairn supports: attestation, attestation withdrawal, key-compromise revocation, introduction, and key rotation. The withdrawal-vs-compromise revocation split is the architectural fix for the cascade-laundering attack per D0006.
- **Issuer-cert-hash binding.** A field in the trust-graph operation envelope that binds each operation to a specific cryptographic identity certificate, enabling per-(issuer, subject) anti-equivocation detection. Without this binding, an adversary controlling a key could issue contradictory attestations to different parties without detection.
- **Nine-field signed-operation schema.** The trust-graph operation envelope structure defined in D0006: operation type, issuer, subject, prior hash, issuer-cert-hash, scope, timestamp, payload, and signature. The schema is stable from v1 and is the substrate for the cascade quarantine semantics.
- **Operational identity.** The keypair that signs day-to-day Cairn operations (capability-token issuance, attestation production). It is hardware-element-gated where the device supports it (StrongBox / Titan M2 on supported Pixels), TEE-backed otherwise, and rotatable on demand or under coercion.
- **Pre-shared peer challenge.** A question-and-answer pair the user and recovery peer agree on out-of-band at provisioning time; the answer is what the peer requires the recovering user to provide before releasing the peer's Shamir share during recovery. Combined with the 48-hour delay-and-confirm window, this is the peer-verification mechanism per [D0005](decisions/D0005-peer-verification.md).
- **Prior-hash chain.** A field in the trust-graph operation envelope that references the hash of the prior operation by the same issuer in the same context, creating an append-only chain per issuer that detects retroactive insertion or removal (§5.2 / D0006).
- **Stale-flag escalation.** The 90-day timer Cairn applies to soft-flagged attestations: if the user does not actively re-confirm a soft-flagged attestation within 90 days, the flag escalates to a stronger quarantine state. The mechanism prevents soft flags from accumulating indefinitely without user attention.
- **Three-tier identity.** Cairn's architectural commitment to separate the master identity (Shamir-split, off-device in routine operation), the operational identity (hardware-element-gated, signs operations, rotatable), and device-scoped capability tokens (short-lived, scoped to specific operations). The model bounds compromise in scope and time rather than total; reconstruction-window and evil-maid surfaces remain (§5.1).
- **Trust graph.** Cairn's data structure of signed attestations, withdrawals, revocations, introductions, and key rotations across the user's social network, anchored in commitment-only Sigsum entries. Each user's trust evaluation is relative to their own attestation set; there is no canonical answer to "is this party trusted" (§5.2).

### B.3 Platforms, protocols, and tools

- **Accrescent.** An Android app distribution channel positioned as an alternative to F-Droid and Google Play, with a focus on application authenticity and reproducible builds. One of Cairn's v1 distribution channels (§5.5).
- **Briar.** A peer-to-peer messaging tool built on Tor, designed for journalists and activists in adversarial network environments. Cairn integrates Briar as the highest-sensitivity tier in v1.5 per [D0004](decisions/D0004-v1-scope-cuts.md). Briar Mailbox (stable since 2023) extends Briar with a store-and-forward component (§2.3).
- **CalyxOS.** A privacy-focused Android-hardening distribution that competes with GrapheneOS. v1 commits to GrapheneOS only; Q26 tracks whether v1.x relaxes this to GrapheneOS-or-CalyxOS.
- **F-Droid.** A long-standing community-operated app distribution channel for open-source Android applications, with its own inclusion criteria and reproducible-build infrastructure. One of Cairn's v1 distribution channels.
- **GrapheneOS.** A privacy- and security-hardened Android distribution that runs on Google Pixel devices; provides hardware-backed verified boot, sandboxed Google Play services, exploit-mitigation hardening, and other defenses Cairn depends on as its endpoint security baseline (§3.4 trust root).
- **Matrix.** A federated end-to-end-encrypted messaging protocol with a strong ecosystem of clients and bridges. Cairn does not federate with Matrix; v4+ may offer optional Matrix integration as an opt-in channel.
- **Meshtastic.** An open-source mesh-radio protocol and ecosystem using LoRa-class radios; supports flood-routing message delivery across multi-hop mesh topologies. Candidate v3 mesh-radio substrate.
- **MeshCore.** An alternative mesh-radio protocol supporting intelligent-routing topologies. Candidate v3 mesh-radio substrate alongside Meshtastic; Cairn intends v3 protocol-agnostic integration if v3 ships.
- **Pixel.** Google's flagship Android phone hardware. The current generation includes the Titan M2 secure element (Pixel 6 onward) which Cairn's StrongBox-backed key storage depends on. Cairn's v1 platform is GrapheneOS-on-Pixel.
- **Rust.** A systems programming language with strong compile-time memory-safety guarantees. Cairn's cryptographic core is in Rust per [D0003](decisions/D0003-implementation-language.md).
- **Session.** A decentralized messaging tool that migrated off the Signal Protocol to its own Session protocol in 2023; uses the Session Network as transport (§2.3).
- **Signal.** A consumer end-to-end-encrypted messenger operated by Signal Foundation (a US Delaware 501(c)(3)). Source for many of the cryptographic patterns Cairn inherits via SimpleX (§2.3).
- **SimpleX.** An identifier-less queue-based messaging protocol with no persistent user identity at the protocol level. Cairn's v1 messaging substrate per §5.4.
- **Tails.** An amnesic Linux distribution (Debian-based) designed to leave no trace on the host computer. Canonical comparator for session-bounded privacy operations; Cairn is the inverse paradigm (persistent cryptographic identity with structural protection of that identity).
- **Threema.** A Swiss-jurisdictional, identifier-less paid messaging product. Closest commercial analogue to Cairn's identifier-less, jurisdiction-aware positioning (§2.3).
- **Titan M2.** A discrete secure element on Pixel 6+ that backs StrongBox key storage. Cairn uses Titan M2 via StrongBox where Ed25519 is supported; falls back to TEE-backed storage otherwise (§4.1).
- **Tor.** The onion-routed anonymity network operated by the Tor Project. Cairn uses Tor as the transport layer for all traffic, with pluggable transports for jurisdictions where Tor itself is subject to DPI blocking (§4.1).
- **Tor pluggable transport.** A protocol obfuscation layer between Tor and the network to evade DPI-based Tor blocking. The pluggable-transport ecosystem (obfs4, meek, snowflake, webtunnel, others) is maintained by the Tor Project and evolves continuously against censor adaptation.
- **TEE (Trusted Execution Environment).** An isolated execution environment within the application processor of a mobile device, providing key storage and operations that the main OS cannot access directly. The fallback for Cairn's hardware-element-gated operational identity where the device does not support StrongBox.
- **UniFFI.** A binding-generation framework (developed by Mozilla) that produces idiomatic foreign-function-interface bindings from a Rust library to other languages (Kotlin, Swift). Cairn uses UniFFI to bridge the Rust core to the Kotlin UI per D0003.
- **UnifiedPush.** An open push-notification protocol designed as an alternative to Google's Firebase Cloud Messaging; users select a distributor (NTFY, others) rather than depending on a single platform vendor. Cairn's push architectural choice when push is enabled (off by default in v1).

### B.4 Threat model and adversary terminology

- **Cellebrite, MSAB, Magnet AXIOM, GrayKey.** Vendor-operated forensic-extraction tools and services that recover data from seized mobile devices, used by border-control, law-enforcement, and intelligence services in many jurisdictions. Named explicitly in §2.1 as part of the threat tier Cairn is designed against.
- **DPI (deep packet inspection).** Network traffic inspection that examines packet content beyond the header, used by ISP-level and state-actor censors to identify and block specific protocols. Tor pluggable transports are designed to evade DPI-based Tor blocking.
- **Duress wipe.** A pattern (used in v1.5 per [D0002](decisions/D0002-duress-profile.md), modeled on GrapheneOS's duress PIN) where entering a specific duress passphrase causes the device to destroy the on-device key material rather than unlocking. Distinguished from _duress profile concealment_ (which Cairn does not implement — detected concealment is itself prosecutable in compelled-decryption jurisdictions).
- **Evil maid attack.** A physical-access attack where an adversary modifies a device — installing a hardware implant, tampering with the boot chain, replacing components — during a window of unattended access. Cairn's tier-separated identity model does not defend the master identity during the reconstruction window or against evil-maid presence (§5.1).
- **Forensic extraction.** The recovery of data from a seized device, typically against full-disk encryption and OS-level protections. Operators include Cellebrite, MSAB, Magnet AXIOM, GrayKey, and similar.
- **HUMINT (human intelligence).** Intelligence collection through human sources — informants, social engineering, infiltration, coerced cooperation. The brief assumes some HUMINT exposure exists for any user with stakes high enough to require Cairn; the trust-graph design specifically limits the blast radius of any single HUMINT compromise (§3.3).
- **IMSI catcher (Stingray, DRT, similar).** A device that impersonates a cellular base station to capture nearby mobile-device identifiers and route mobile traffic through the attacker's infrastructure. Cairn's protection against IMSI-catcher data collection comes from Tor as the transport layer plus the identifier-less queue protocol; the metadata IMSI catchers collect from the cellular layer is outside Cairn's mitigation surface.
- **Mercenary spyware.** Commercial offensive cyber capabilities sold to state and quasi-state buyers (NSO Group's Pegasus; Intellexa's Predator; Cytrox / Saito Tech; Candiru / Sourgum; Memento Labs; and others) and deployed against civil-society targets including journalists, activists, and dissidents. Documented extensively by Citizen Lab and Amnesty International Security Lab.
- **Pegasus, Predator, Candiru, Sourgum.** Specific mercenary-spyware products. Named in §2.1 with examples of jurisdictions where civil-society targets have been compromised by these tools.
- **Recovery network surface (§3.3).** The cryptographic exposure that arises when an adversary identifies and compromises a user's recovery peers: 3-of-5 successful compromises yield the user's master cryptographic identity even if the user is not directly compromised. The architectural tradeoff of social recovery as an answer to the lack of friendly-jurisdiction trustees.
- **Side-channel attack.** Extracting information from a system through unintended observable channels (timing, power consumption, cache state, EM emanation) rather than through the intended interface. Cairn does not specifically mitigate side-channel attacks beyond the standard practice of using constant-time primitives where available.

### B.5 Operations, governance, and funding

- **ADR (Architectural Decision Record).** An ADR-style document records a specific decision with its context, the decision itself, alternatives considered, consequences, and references. Cairn's decisions live in `docs/decisions/` as D0001 through D0014; see Appendix A.
- **BYOD (Bring Your Own Device).** The pilot model where pilot users source their own GrapheneOS-capable Pixel devices through standard commercial channels rather than receiving project-provisioned hardware (§10.1).
- **Dead-man's-switch check-in.** The monthly developer-availability signal Cairn commits to publishing per [D0009](decisions/D0009-sudden-unavailability.md); after 60 days of silence, a pre-arranged partner organization is empowered to publish a project status advisory.
- **Fiscal sponsor.** A non-profit organization that holds tax-exempt status and accepts grants on behalf of unincorporated projects, taking a percentage as administrative fees (typically 5–15% per §10.2). Cairn anticipates using a fiscal sponsor for grant intake during the 18–24 month pre-incorporation window per [D0010](decisions/D0010-foundation-jurisdiction.md).
- **Honorarium.** Compensation paid for services rendered in a context where market-rate billing would be inappropriate or where the relationship is not transactional (e.g., reviewer attestation services). Cairn's reviewer-honoraria operating model is described in §8.2; Phase B/C funding gates apply per §10.3.
- **MVP (Minimum Viable Product).** The smallest cut of a product that delivers value to its target audience. v1 is Cairn's MVP per the §6.1 scope and the v1 architecture per §5.
- **No-skip-the-audit posture.** The brief's structural commitment per [D0011](decisions/D0011-audit-budget-and-timing.md) that v1 pilot does not deploy without the pre-pilot cryptographic-primitives audit closing; broader-than-pilot release does not happen without the pre-beta full audit closing.
- **Open-questions.md (Q1–Q26).** The brief's open-questions tracker for items deferred or unresolved; each question has status (Open / Resolved / Reserved / Withdrawn) and links to its blocking decision-document if resolved.
- **Phase A / Phase B / Phase C / Phase D.** Cairn's funding-phase model per §10. Phase A is volunteer baseline (no external funding required); Phase B is the first-dollar threshold (~$20–60K addressable; unlocks pilot readiness); Phase C is pre-broader-release funding (~$105–405K; unlocks broader-than-pilot release); Phase D is steady-state operations (~$90–250K/year excluding maintainer compensation, which is aspirational).
- **Quorum (3-of-5 attestation).** The threshold at which Cairn releases ship under the §5.5 / 8.2 release-security model: at least three of five recruited external reviewers attest before a release is published. The 3-of-5 threshold is sized to tolerate partial reviewer-pool churn while requiring honest-majority attestation.
- **Reviewer pool (v1.5 ship target per [D0015](decisions/D0015-v1-release-security-posture.md)).** The 5+ external reviewers Cairn commits to recruiting (per §8.6, conditional on Q5 partner outreach; honoraria operations Q3-conditional) to attest each release with a 3-of-5 attestation threshold. Pool recruitment, rotation, and honoraria are described in §8.2. At v1, the recruited pool is not yet a trust root — v1 release security relies on developer source review plus the witness-cosigned release log plus F-Droid distribution (the v1.5-rebuild-attestation substrate). Recruitment work proceeds at v1 through Q5 outreach; willing reviewers may soft-ship attestations against v1 releases. The pool's architectural-commitment role activates at v1.5 alongside reproducible builds, delivering binary-equivalence multi-party verification at v1.5+. The volunteer-baseline cadence per [D0008](decisions/D0008-volunteer-baseline-cadence.md) governs ship timing at both v1 (engineering + audit + consent protocol gates) and v1.5+ (pool-quorum-formation gate).
- **Safe Harbor.** A formal commitment by a project not to pursue legal action against security researchers disclosing in good faith. Cairn's posture per [D0012](decisions/D0012-researcher-safe-harbor.md) is _stated intent_ until foundation incorporation; formal Safe Harbor language (disclose.io, Bugcrowd "We Will Not Sue", or EFF Coders' Rights Project template) lands at incorporation per Q16.
- **Sigsum witness pool.** The set of partner organizations that cosign Sigsum log entries to make log tampering detectable. Recruitment is the project's responsibility per §8.6, conditional on partner outreach; the same witnesses cosign both the trust-graph audit log and the release-binary audit log, with the shared-witness-pool concentration acknowledged as a correlation risk in §3.4.
- **501(c)(3), Stichting, Verein, Aktiengesellschaft, CIC.** Non-profit legal-entity forms in different jurisdictions (US 501(c)(3); Dutch Stichting; Swiss Verein or AG; UK Community Interest Company). Candidates for foundation incorporation per [D0010](decisions/D0010-foundation-jurisdiction.md); selection deferred to legal consultation.

### B.6 Organizations and acronyms

- **Citizen Lab.** A research lab at the University of Toronto's Munk School that investigates digital threats against civil society. Source of much of the public Pegasus and Predator targeting documentation Cairn references.
- **Cure53.** A Berlin-based information-security firm known for civil-society security audits at mission-org rates. Named as a candidate audit firm per [D0011](decisions/D0011-audit-budget-and-timing.md).
- **EFF (Electronic Frontier Foundation).** A US-based digital-rights non-profit. Operates the Coders' Rights Project (one of the candidate Safe Harbor templates for Q16) and Threat Lab (research and pilot-mediation candidate per §8.6).
- **FPF (Freedom of the Press Foundation).** A US-based non-profit operating SecureDrop and supporting press-freedom causes. Adjacent comparator landscape per §2.3.
- **IRB (Institutional Review Board).** A research-ethics body that reviews proposed research involving human subjects; "IRB-equivalent" in the brief refers to the academic-research-style consent and exit protocols Cairn's pilot adopts via [D0013](decisions/D0013-pilot-consent-exit.md).
- **MSAB.** A Swedish forensic-extraction vendor (XRY product line); peer to Cellebrite in border-control and law-enforcement deployments.
- **NCC Group.** A UK-headquartered global information-security firm. Named as a candidate audit firm per D0011.
- **NGO (Non-Governmental Organization).** A non-profit organization independent of government, typically with a social, humanitarian, or political mission. Multiple candidate Cairn partner organizations are NGOs (Tactical Tech, Front Line Defenders, Access Now, others).
- **NLnet Foundation.** A Netherlands-based foundation operating funded calls (NGI Zero, NGI Zero Trust) for European-jurisdiction-friendly open-source security and infrastructure projects. Named as a candidate funder and a potential fiscal-sponsor / grantee-sponsorship route per §10.5.
- **NSO Group.** An Israeli mercenary-spyware vendor (Pegasus product). Named in §2.1 with documented targeting examples.
- **OCF (Open Collective Foundation), OSC (Open Source Collective).** Lower-overhead fiscal-sponsor candidates per [D0010](decisions/D0010-foundation-jurisdiction.md).
- **OTF (Open Technology Fund).** A US-based independent funder of internet freedom and security tools; operates the Secure Audit programme and main grant lines Cairn is positioned to apply to.
- **Quarkslab.** A French information-security firm known for cryptographic-primitive audits. Named as a candidate audit firm per D0011.
- **SFC (Software Freedom Conservancy).** A US-based 501(c)(3) hosting fiscal-sponsorship arrangements for free-software projects, with experience in security-tool partnerships. Candidate fiscal sponsor per D0010.
- **Tactical Tech.** A Berlin-based non-profit supporting civil-society security through training, research, and toolkits (Security in-a-Box). Candidate Cairn partner organization per §8.6.
- **Trail of Bits.** A US-based information-security firm known for cryptographic-primitive audits at commercial and civic-tech rates. Named as a candidate audit firm per D0011.

### B.7 Brief-internal vocabulary

- **Architecture-vs-audience honesty.** The brief's discipline of naming where the architectural commitments do and do not serve specific populations within the threat-tier audience, rather than claiming uniform audience reach. Surfaced in §2.2 (audience three-layer model) and [D0014](decisions/D0014-non-peer-recovery.md).
- **Bounded-window exposure.** The §5.1 framing for the master identity: outside the brief reconstruction windows at provisioning and recovery, the master is not on the device to extract. _Not_ "the master is never exposed" — which would be an overstatement. See §4.2.
- **Calibrated language.** The §4.2 design principle that replaces absolute-sounding claims ("verified through chain of attestations" rather than "secure"; "raises the cost of" rather than "defeats"). Applied throughout the brief, with the §4 adversarial review's verb-deflation sweep landing in v0.2.
- **Conditional commitment.** A commitment the brief makes that depends on conditions outside the project's unilateral control (funding closing, partner outreach succeeding, upstream maintenance continuing). The §8 register makes this distinction explicit and the brief avoids "commits to" phrasing for items that are actually conditional.
- **Layered resistance.** The §5.3 framing for the peer-verification mechanism: pre-shared challenges plus the 48-hour delay-and-confirm window combine to raise the cost of the unlock → peer enumeration → impersonation chain. _Not_ "defeats" the chain.
- **Phase-gate register.** The §7.1 / §10.1 framing where releases and operational milestones are described by their unlocking conditions rather than by calendar dates ("v1.5 ships when Phase C funding closes and foundation incorporation is materially in progress" rather than "v1.5 ships approximately 6–9 months post-v1").
- **Trust substitution, not trust elimination.** The §4.3 framing for Cairn's release-security stack: the developer's single signing identity is replaced with a distributed trust set (reviewer pool + witness pool + OIDC provider integrity) rather than removed. The architectural property is the substitution being publicly auditable; trust is moved, not eliminated.
- **Unilateral commitment.** A commitment the brief makes that the project can fulfill without external dependencies (the GitHub repository being public; the decision-document register being maintained; the disclosure policy being honored at the project's own discretion). The §8 register distinguishes these from conditional commitments above.

---

## Appendix C: References

_Purpose: cite the prior work, standards, threat intelligence, and external projects the brief draws on. The reference list is organized by category and is non-exhaustive — it captures the principal sources the brief's claims rest against rather than every adjacent citation. A reader using this appendix to verify specific brief claims should consult the inline cross-references in §§3–10 first; this appendix is the consolidated catalog._

### C.1 Cryptographic standards and primitives

- **RFC 8032 — Edwards-curve Digital Signature Algorithm (EdDSA).** Defines Ed25519 and Ed448 signatures. <https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc8032>
- **RFC 7748 — Elliptic Curves for Security.** Defines Curve25519 and Curve448. <https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc7748>
- **RFC 8439 — ChaCha20 and Poly1305 for IETF Protocols.** Defines the AEAD construction Cairn uses for symmetric authenticated encryption. <https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc8439>
- **RFC 8949 — Concise Binary Object Representation (CBOR).** Section 4.2.1 defines the deterministic encoding rules Cairn relies on for signed-CBOR reproducibility. <https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc8949>
- **RFC 9052 — CBOR Object Signing and Encryption (COSE) Structures and Process.** Cairn's capability tokens and trust-graph operation envelopes are COSE_Sign1 structures. <https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9052>
- **RFC 9420 — The Messaging Layer Security (MLS) Protocol.** Referenced as the standard Matrix is migrating to and as the protocol Wire uses. <https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9420>
- **Shamir, A. (1979). "How to share a secret."** _Communications of the ACM_ 22(11): 612–613. The foundational paper for Shamir Secret Sharing. <https://doi.org/10.1145/359168.359176>
- **SLIP-39 — Shamir's Secret-Sharing for Mnemonic Codes.** A standardized share format Cairn evaluates as an alternative to custom share formatting. <https://github.com/satoshilabs/slips/blob/master/slip-0039.md>

### C.2 Protocol references

- **Signal Protocol specifications.** Documentation for the X3DH key agreement and double-ratchet algorithm Cairn's messaging protocol descends from via SimpleX. <https://signal.org/docs/>
- **SimpleX protocol documentation.** The identifier-less queue protocol Cairn uses as the v1 messaging substrate. <https://github.com/simplex-chat/simplex-chat/blob/master/docs/protocol/simplex-messaging.md>
- **Briar protocol documentation.** Peer-to-peer-over-Tor messaging protocol Cairn integrates as the v1.5 highest-sensitivity tier. <https://code.briarproject.org/briar/briar/-/wikis/home>
- **Briar Mailbox.** Store-and-forward extension to Briar (stable 2023) acknowledged in §2.3's Briar characterization. <https://briarproject.org/manual/mailbox/>
- **Cwtch.** Peer-to-peer-over-Tor messaging with untrusted-group-server pattern; comparator considered in §5.4. <https://cwtch.im>
- **Matrix specification and MLS migration (MSC4191 and related MSCs).** Matrix protocol documentation and the in-progress MLS migration tracked in §2.3. <https://spec.matrix.org/> and <https://github.com/matrix-org/matrix-spec-proposals>
- **WhatsApp Auditable Key Directory (AKD).** WhatsApp's transparency-log-anchored key directory implementation, referenced in §4.3 as prior art for transparency-logged key state. <https://engineering.fb.com/2023/04/13/security/whatsapp-key-transparency/>
- **iMessage Contact Key Verification (CKV).** Apple's transparency-log-anchored contact key verification, referenced in §4.3 as prior art for transparency-logged key state. <https://security.apple.com/blog/imessage-contact-key-verification/>
- **CONIKS: Bringing Key Transparency to End Users (Melara et al., 2015).** Academic origin for transparency-log-anchored key directories. <https://www.usenix.org/conference/usenixsecurity15/technical-sessions/presentation/melara>

### C.3 Sigstore, Sigsum, and supply-chain provenance

- **Sigstore project.** Identity-based signing infrastructure (Fulcio for OIDC-bound certificate issuance; Rekor for transparency logging; cosign for signing operations). <https://www.sigstore.dev>
- **Sigstore specifications.** Specifications for the Fulcio certificate format, Rekor entry formats, and cosign verification semantics. <https://docs.sigstore.dev>
- **Sigsum project.** Witness-cosigned transparency log infrastructure with minimalist operational requirements. <https://www.sigsum.org>
- **Sigsum project documentation and witness-pool design.** <https://git.glasklar.is/sigsum/project/documentation>
- **The Update Framework (TUF).** Reference framework for secure software update systems; considered in §5.5 architectural alternatives. <https://theupdateframework.io>
- **Reproducible Builds.** The project, methodologies, and tooling for reproducible-build verification. <https://reproducible-builds.org>
- **APK Signature Scheme v3.** Android's APK signing format that supports key rotation, referenced in §5.5 for the long-lived APK key compromise-recovery process. <https://source.android.com/docs/security/features/apksigning/v3>

### C.4 Tor, anonymization, and pluggable transports

- **The Tor Project.** Documentation, specifications, and ongoing roadmap for the Tor anonymization network. <https://www.torproject.org>
- **Tor Pluggable Transports.** Specifications and implementations of DPI-evasion transport layers (obfs4, meek, snowflake, webtunnel). <https://www.pluggabletransports.info>
- **Arti — A Rust Tor implementation.** The Rust-native Tor client implementation Cairn prefers per D0003. <https://gitlab.torproject.org/tpo/core/arti>

### C.5 GrapheneOS, Android hardening, and hardware

- **GrapheneOS.** Project documentation including security model, attestation, and hardened components. <https://grapheneos.org>
- **GrapheneOS threat model and security features.** <https://grapheneos.org/features>
- **CalyxOS.** Alternative privacy-focused Android distribution evaluated in §2.3 and Q26. <https://calyxos.org>
- **Pixel security documentation (Google).** Titan M2 secure-element documentation; StrongBox-backed Keystore documentation. <https://www.gstatic.com/pixel/security-docs/>
- **Android Keystore — Hardware-Backed Keystore documentation.** <https://source.android.com/docs/security/features/keystore>

### C.6 Threat research and adversary documentation

- **Citizen Lab — Pegasus targeting reports.** A multi-year corpus of investigations into mercenary-spyware deployments against civil-society targets. <https://citizenlab.ca/category/research/targeted-threats/>
- **Citizen Lab — Predator targeting reports.** Investigations into Intellexa's Predator spyware deployment, including the Greek "Predatorgate" reporting. <https://citizenlab.ca/2023/10/predator-in-the-wires-ahmed-eltantawy-targeted-with-predator-spyware-after-announcing-presidential-ambitions/>
- **Amnesty International Security Lab.** Forensic documentation of mercenary-spyware targeting, including the Pegasus Project consortium with Forbidden Stories. <https://securitylab.amnesty.org>
- **The Pegasus Project (Forbidden Stories consortium).** Coordinated investigative reporting on Pegasus targeting across multiple jurisdictions. <https://forbiddenstories.org/case/the-pegasus-project/>
- **Access Now Digital Security Helpline.** Civil-society incident response and threat-intelligence resource. <https://www.accessnow.org/help/>
- **EFF Threat Lab.** Research on spyware and surveillance targeting civil society. <https://www.eff.org/issues/security>
- **Cellebrite — public documentation and product specifications.** Forensic-extraction tools referenced in §2.1 threat tier. <https://cellebrite.com>
- **MSAB (XRY product line) — public documentation.** Forensic-extraction tools. <https://www.msab.com>

### C.7 Civil-society security toolkits and methodologies

- **Tactical Tech.** Toolkits, training, and research on digital security for civil society; Security in-a-Box. <https://tacticaltech.org> and <https://securityinabox.org>
- **Front Line Defenders.** Protection-work guidance and casework support for at-risk human-rights defenders. <https://www.frontlinedefenders.org>
- **Access Now.** Policy, digital-security helpline, and grants programmes. <https://www.accessnow.org>
- **EFF Surveillance Self-Defense.** Digital-security guidance for at-risk users. <https://ssd.eff.org>
- **Citizen Lab research-ethics framework.** Academic-research-style protocols for working with at-risk subjects; one of the candidate frameworks for D0013 pilot consent and exit protocol selection. <https://citizenlab.ca>
- **Internews — Protection-tech evaluation guidance.** Civil-society-tooling evaluation methodology referenced in D0013 framework selection. <https://internews.org>
- **SecureDrop.** Source-protection submission system operated by Freedom of the Press Foundation. <https://securedrop.org>

### C.8 Implementation libraries and tools

- **Rust crates referenced in D0003 / D0006:**
  - **`coset`** — COSE implementation for Rust. <https://crates.io/crates/coset>
  - **`zeroize`** — Secret-material lifetime control. <https://crates.io/crates/zeroize>
  - **`secrecy`** — Wrapping types for secret-material handling. <https://crates.io/crates/secrecy>
  - **`subtle`** — Constant-time primitives. <https://crates.io/crates/subtle>
  - **`vsss-rs`** — Shamir Secret Sharing implementation candidate. <https://crates.io/crates/vsss-rs>
- **UniFFI.** Mozilla's binding-generation framework for Rust↔ {Kotlin, Swift, Python} interop. <https://mozilla.github.io/uniffi-rs/>
- **`arti`** — Rust-native Tor client implementation. See C.4.

### C.9 Audit firms (cited as candidates in D0011)

- **Trail of Bits.** US-based information-security firm with cryptographic-primitive audit practice; public reports at <https://github.com/trailofbits/publications>
- **NCC Group.** UK-headquartered global information-security firm with cryptography services practice. <https://www.nccgroup.com/research>
- **Cure53.** Berlin-based information-security firm with civil-society audit history at mission-org rates. <https://cure53.de>
- **Quarkslab.** French information-security firm with cryptographic-primitive audit experience. <https://www.quarkslab.com>

### C.10 Funders and grant programmes

- **Open Technology Fund — Secure Audit programme.** <https://www.opentech.fund/funds/secure-audit/>
- **Open Technology Fund — main grant programmes.** <https://www.opentech.fund>
- **NLnet Foundation — NGI Zero Trust.** <https://nlnet.nl/NGI0Entrust/>
- **NLnet Foundation — NGI Zero programmes and main funded calls.** <https://nlnet.nl>
- **Mozilla Open Source Support (MOSS).** <https://www.mozilla.org/en-US/moss/>
- **Mozilla Open Source Audit Awards (OSAA history).** <https://blog.mozilla.org/security/category/audits/>
- **Ford Foundation — Technology and Society programme.** <https://www.fordfoundation.org/work/our-grants/build/global-trustworthy-internet/>
- **Open Society Foundations — Information and Digital Rights.** <https://www.opensocietyfoundations.org/what-we-do/themes/information-and-digital-rights>
- **Knight Foundation — Journalism programmes.** <https://knightfoundation.org/program/journalism/>
- **Sloan Foundation — Better Software for Science programme** (referenced in §10.5 multi-year engineering-capacity grant category). <https://sloan.org/programs/digital-technology/better-software-for-science>
- **Chan Zuckerberg Initiative — Essential Open Source Software for Science.** <https://chanzuckerberg.com/eoss/>
- **Internet Society Foundation.** <https://www.isocfoundation.org>

### C.11 Fiscal sponsors and foundation infrastructure (cited as candidates in D0010)

- **Software Freedom Conservancy.** <https://sfconservancy.org>
- **Open Collective Foundation / Open Source Collective.** <https://opencollective.com> and <https://oscollective.org>
- **Code for Science & Society.** <https://codeforscience.org>
- **NumFOCUS.** <https://numfocus.org>
- **NLnet Foundation** (operates grantee-sponsorship in addition to grantmaking). See C.10.

### C.12 Researcher protection templates (cited as candidates in Q16 / D0012)

- **disclose.io.** Open-source Safe Harbor template widely adopted across security-tools projects. <https://disclose.io>
- **Bugcrowd "We Will Not Sue" disclosure terms.** <https://www.bugcrowd.com/resources/standard-disclosure-terms/>
- **EFF Coders' Rights Project.** <https://www.eff.org/issues/coders/legal-defense-toolkit>

### C.13 Distribution channels

- **F-Droid.** Community-operated app distribution and reproducible-build infrastructure for open-source Android. <https://f-droid.org>
- **Accrescent.** Alternative Android distribution channel focused on application authenticity. <https://accrescent.app>

### C.14 Regulatory frameworks referenced

- **US Export Administration Regulations (EAR).** Encryption-export framework. <https://www.bis.doc.gov/index.php/regulations/export-administration-regulations-ear>
- **EU Dual Use Regulation (EU 2021/821).** European encryption-export framework. <https://eur-lex.europa.eu/legal-content/EN/TXT/?uri=CELEX%3A02021R0821>
- **Wassenaar Arrangement.** Multilateral export-control regime including encryption and intrusion-software controls. <https://www.wassenaar.org>
- **UK Regulation of Investigatory Powers Act 2000 (RIPA).** Compelled-decryption provisions Cairn references in §3.3. <https://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2000/23/contents>
- **Australia Telecommunications and Other Legislation Amendment (Assistance and Access) Act 2018 (TOLA).** Industry-assistance regime Cairn references in §3.3. <https://www.legislation.gov.au/Details/C2018A00148>
- **France Article 434-15-2 of the Code pénal.** Compelled-disclosure provision Cairn references in §3.3. <https://www.legifrance.gouv.fr/codes/article_lc/LEGIARTI000030939438/>

### C.15 Reproducible-build, supply-chain, and signing references

- **Reproducible Builds project.** See C.3.
- **Debian Reproducible Builds.** <https://wiki.debian.org/ReproducibleBuilds>
- **NixOS reproducibility tracking.** <https://nixos.org/manual/nixos/stable/#sec-reproducibility>
- **Briar reproducible-build documentation.** <https://code.briarproject.org/briar/briar-reproducer>
- **Signal Android reproducible-build documentation.** <https://github.com/signalapp/Signal-Android/tree/main/reproducible-builds>

### C.16 Civil-society security incident corpora

- **Citizen Lab — TargetedThreats research index.** <https://citizenlab.ca/category/research/targeted-threats/>
- **Amnesty International Security Lab — research index.** <https://securitylab.amnesty.org/research/>
- **Mercenary spyware accountability and trade documentation.** Multiple researcher consortia documenting NSO Group, Intellexa, Candiru, Memento Labs, and related vendors (Citizen Lab corpus above is the canonical entry point).

### C.17 Editorial and writing standards

- **Strunk, W. & White, E.B. — _The Elements of Style._** The diction discipline the brief's calibration commitments echo: precise, calibrated, honest verb selection.
- **Architectural Decision Records (ADRs) — community documentation.** The ADR pattern Cairn's decision register uses. <https://adr.github.io>

## Document changelog

- **0.5 (2026-05-28).** Architecture-simplification adversarial review Section A consensus cuts applied (F1, F2, F3, F12, F17, F19). F1: project-operated SimpleX crash-reporting queue cut from v1; pilot crash reports route through D0013 partner-mediated channel. F2: multi-target build pipeline cut from v1; v1 produces GrapheneOS-Pixel APK only; cross-compilation for v2/v3 deferred to v2 work. F3: property-based migration test framework deferred to v1.5; schema-versioning fields ship v1 with basic round-trip tests, framework lands with first real migration at v1.5. F12: UnifiedPush distributor-selection UX deferred to v1.5; v1 ships polling-only with no in-app distributor UX. F17: §5.5/§6.1 distribution-channel inconsistency reconciled; Tor onion service operation and offline signed images deferred from v1 to v1.5+ to match §6.1's narrower scope. F19: new §10.4 Phase D operational developer-time line items added (upstream-roadmap tracking; witness-pool / reviewer-pool coordination; test-infrastructure maintenance; partner-organization coordination) honestly accounting for the ~190-440 hours/year operational load the developer absorbs at the volunteer baseline. D0004 expanded with items 5-8 absorbing the four cuts.
- **0.4 (2026-05-28).** Architecture-simplification adversarial review F6 applied: foundation incorporation deferred from v1 / Phase C scope with v1.5 broader-release evaluation trigger (new D0016). Five trigger criteria (pilot evidence of structural-mitigation need; funding scale crossing fiscal-sponsor-vs-foundation-overhead breakeven; funder requirement; personal-liability scenario; structural-mitigation cascade) with two-of-five activation threshold. Default operational structure for duration of deferral is fiscal-sponsor arrangement; D0009 partner advisory authority becomes permanent governance scaffold. D0010 / D0012 framing updates: jurisdictional analysis substrate persists for if-trigger-activates path; Safe Harbor remains published-preference indefinitely under deferral. §10 phase model updates: Phase C ranges split by trigger outcome; Phase D operates under either foundation-operating or fiscal-sponsor-operating posture with structurally different line items; fiscal-sponsor fee permanent under deferral rather than transitional. §8.4 Path to foundation substantially rewritten. Q14 / Q15 elevated to "permanent operational" status; Q16 deferred indefinitely under D0016. §10.7 funding risks reframed: "D0016 trigger does not activate" is expected operational state, not failure mode.
- **0.3 (2026-05-28).** §1 second-pass adversarial review applied (24 findings: parameter error "5-of-N" → "3-of-5 over 5+ pool"; "honest"/"honestly" pile-up reduced 5→0; subsection headers §1.1–§1.7 promoted; phase-funding table; reader-intent navigation map for funders/partners/researchers/pilot candidates; new non-promise disclaimers — gross-of-fiscal-sponsor-fees, BYOD jurisdictional channel availability, runway gap as documented §9.1-to-§10 breach; landscape-dating disclaim). Architecture-simplification adversarial review applied F4: recruited 5+/3-of-5 reviewer pool deferred from v1 critical path to v1.5 alongside reproducible builds (per new D0015). v1 release-security stack: developer Sigstore identity-based signing + Rekor + Sigsum-anchored release log with witness cosignatures + multi-channel distribution (F-Droid primary) + developer source review. §4.3 differentiation reframed from "four architectural commitments" to "three commitments + a v1 release-security posture honestly described relative to comparable open-source security tools (Briar, F-Droid, GrapheneOS, Signal Android)" with v1.5 expansion to "additionally distinct from Briar via recruited-pool + reproducible-builds combination." D0004, D0008, D0011 minor revisions; Q5, Q10 partial-resolution updates. Q1–Q26 unchanged in count.
- **0.2 (2026-05-28).** Substantial post-adversarial-review revision cycle. New: §1 Executive Summary (synthesis pass); §10 Funding and Resourcing (phase-gated cost model); D0008–D0014 decision documents; Q13–Q26 open questions; per-lens adversarial review artifacts under `docs/reviews/`; consolidated review documents for §§2, 4, 6/7, 8/9, 10. Major: §2 audience three-layer restructure with co-located adversary / non-peer-recovery acknowledgments; §4 calibration sweep (verb deflation, trust-substitution-not-elimination, dependency-surface naming); §§6/7 phase-gate register replacing calendar windows; §6.1 solo-developer specialist-absorption and v1 cryptographic-engineering enumeration; §3.3 supply-chain BYOD decomposition; §10 internal-contradiction fixes (BYOD reconciliation; reviewer-honoraria phase split; foundation-incorporation dependency; addressable-by-instrument floor framing; named-ask §10.9; sustainability-cliff acknowledgment in §10.4); §10.8 disclaimer set expansion; §2.3 landscape calendar pass with Tails/SecureDrop/CalyxOS/Threema/Wire/Olvid additions and Wickr/Signal/Matrix/Briar/Session/SimpleX updates. Appendix A rewritten as decision-document index + thematic groupings + interaction chains; Appendix B rewritten as comprehensive thematic glossary including brief-internal vocabulary; Appendix C rewritten as structured reference catalog.
- **0.1 (2026-05-27 / earlier).** Initial outline transferred from prior conversation; scaffold structure based on architecture decisions to date; §§3, 5 drafted and adversarially reviewed; D0001–D0007 decision documents; Q1–Q12 open questions; placeholders for §§1–2, §§6–10, appendices.
